# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes RBAC ClusterRole Privilege Escalation Paths

## Your Task

Audit kubernetes/kubernetes for RBAC privilege escalation paths. Find all Go source files that validate ClusterRole escalation rules — specifically, the files that enforce the 'escalation' verb restriction and prevent users from granting permissions they don't hold.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [

  ],
  "symbols": [

  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive audit of Kubernetes' RBAC privilege escalation prevention paths. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

The Kubernetes RBAC system implements escalation prevention through a layered approach with **12 critical files** and **17 key functions/types**:

### Core Escalation Checks
1. **escalation_check.go** - Three gatekeeping functions:
   - `EscalationAllowed()` - Exempts system:masters (superusers)
   - `RoleEscalationAuthorized()` - Checks if user has "escalate" verb on roles
   - `BindingAuthorized()` - Checks if user has "bind" verb

### Storage Layer Enforcement
2. **Four policybased storage implementations** enforce rules at write time:
   - ClusterRole and Role storage validate rule permissions
   - ClusterRoleBinding and RoleBinding storage validate binding permissions
   - All check for escalation via `ConfirmNoEscalation()` before allowing creation/updates

### Validation Engine
3. **rule.go** - `ConfirmNoEscalation()` is the core validation function that:
   - Resolves the user's current permissions
   - Uses `Covers()` to verify the user can grant the requested permissions
   - Returns detailed error messages listing what permissions are missing

### Policy Comparison
4. **policy_comparator.go** - The algorithmic core:
   - `Covers()` - Breaks rules down to atomic components
   - `ruleCovers()` - Verifies coverage with wildcard matching support
   - Handles verbs, resources, resource names, and non-resource URLs

### Supporting Infrastructure
5. **policy_compact.go** - Compacts granular missing rules for readable errors
6. **helpers.go** - Allows GC-related updates to bypass checks

don't currently hold. The core implementation spans several key areas:\\n\\n1. **Escalation Authorization Layer (pkg/registry/rbac/escalation_check.go):** The foundation consists of three critical functions: EscalationAllowed() checks if the user is part of system:masters (superusers), RoleEscalationAuthorized() verifies the user has the 'escalate' verb permission on role/clusterrole resources, and BindingAuthorized() checks the 'bind' verb for role/clusterrole resources. These functions work together to determine whether privilege escalation checks should be bypassed entirely (for superusers) or enforced (for regular users).\\n\\n2. **Storage Layer Enforcement (policybased storage files):** Four policybased storage packages enforce escalation rules at write time:\\n   - pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrole/policybased/storage.go: Controls ClusterRole creation/updates, blocking users from granting rule combinations they don't possess. For aggregated cluster roles, it enforces full cluster-admin privileges (via fullAuthority check) since aggregation rules can gather any permissions.\\n   - pkg/registry/rbac/role/policybased/storage.go: Similar enforcement for namespaced Roles.\\n   - pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrolebinding/policybased/storage.go: Prevents users from binding cluster roles unless they either have the 'bind' verb or already possess all permissions in the target role.\\n   - pkg/registry/rbac/rolebinding/policybased/storage.go: Equivalent namespaced binding enforcement.\\n\\n3. **Validation Logic (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go):** The ConfirmNoEscalation() function is the workhorse of escalation prevention. It retrieves the user's current permissions via AuthorizationRuleResolver, then uses the Covers() function to verify that the user's existing permissions completely cover the rules they're trying to grant. If any permission gaps exist, the operation is forbidden with detailed error messages listing the missing rights.\\n\\n4. **Internal Version Support (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/internal_version_adapter.go):** The ConfirmNoEscalationInternal() function adapts internal API version rules to v1 format before validation, ensuring consistency across different API versions.\\n\\n5. **Policy Comparison Engine (staging/src/k8s.io/component-helpers/auth/rbac/validation/policy_comparator.go):** The Covers() function is the algorithmic core of escalation prevention. It breaks down rules to their atomic components (verb, resource, resource name, API group) via BreakdownRule() and verifies each subrule is covered by at least one of the user's rules via ruleCovers(). The ruleCovers() function handles wildcard matching (verbs, resources, non-resource URLs) and resource name restrictions.\\n\\n6. **Error Reporting (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/policy_compact.go):** The CompactRules() function consolidates granular missing permission rules into a human-readable format, combining rules that differ only by verb to improve error message clarity.\\n\\n7. **Garbage Collection Handling (pkg/registry/rbac/helpers.go):** The IsOnlyMutatingGCFields() function allows GC-related updates (finalizers, owner references, managed fields) to bypass escalation checks, preventing unnecessary permission escalation denials during object deletion.\\n\\n8. **Admission Policy Integration:** Additional authorization checks in mutatingadmissionpolicy/authz.go and mutatingadmissionpolicybinding/authz.go use EscalationAllowed() to bypass checks for superusers, maintaining consistency across admission control.\\n\\nThe escalation checking flow is: User attempts to create/modify a role or binding \u2192 Storage layer checks if EscalationAllowed (superuser) or RoleEscalationAuthorized (has escalate permission) \u2192 If not, calls ConfirmNoEscalation/ConfirmNoEscalationInternal \u2192 Retrieves user's current permissions via DefaultRuleResolver \u2192 Compares via Covers() using atomic rule breakdown \u2192 Returns forbidden if any permissions are missing, with detailed missing rights information.\\n\\nThis design ensures that the 'escalate' verb acts as a gating mechanism - while normal users cannot grant permissions they don't have, users with explicit 'escalate' permission on roles/clusterroles can grant any permissions, providing a controlled escape hatch for role administrators.\"\n}\n",

don't currently hold. The core implementation spans several key areas:\\n\\n1. **Escalation Authorization Layer (pkg/registry/rbac/escalation_check.go):** The foundation consists of three critical functions: EscalationAllowed() checks if the user is part of system:masters (superusers), RoleEscalationAuthorized() verifies the user has the 'escalate' verb permission on role/clusterrole resources, and BindingAuthorized() checks the 'bind' verb for role/clusterrole resources. These functions work together to determine whether privilege escalation checks should be bypassed entirely (for superusers) or enforced (for regular users).\\n\\n2. **Storage Layer Enforcement (policybased storage files):** Four policybased storage packages enforce escalation rules at write time:\\n   - pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrole/policybased/storage.go: Controls ClusterRole creation/updates, blocking users from granting rule combinations they don't possess. For aggregated cluster roles, it enforces full cluster-admin privileges (via fullAuthority check) since aggregation rules can gather any permissions.\\n   - pkg/registry/rbac/role/policybased/storage.go: Similar enforcement for namespaced Roles.\\n   - pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrolebinding/policybased/storage.go: Prevents users from binding cluster roles unless they either have the 'bind' verb or already possess all permissions in the target role.\\n   - pkg/registry/rbac/rolebinding/policybased/storage.go: Equivalent namespaced binding enforcement.\\n\\n3. **Validation Logic (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go):** The ConfirmNoEscalation() function is the workhorse of escalation prevention. It retrieves the user's current permissions via AuthorizationRuleResolver, then uses the Covers() function to verify that the user's existing permissions completely cover the rules they're trying to grant. If any permission gaps exist, the operation is forbidden with detailed error messages listing the missing rights.\\n\\n4. **Internal Version Support (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/internal_version_adapter.go):** The ConfirmNoEscalationInternal() function adapts internal API version rules to v1 format before validation, ensuring consistency across different API versions.\\n\\n5. **Policy Comparison Engine (staging/src/k8s.io/component-helpers/auth/rbac/validation/policy_comparator.go):** The Covers() function is the algorithmic core of escalation prevention. It breaks down rules to their atomic components (verb, resource, resource name, API group) via BreakdownRule() and verifies each subrule is covered by at least one of the user's rules via ruleCovers(). The ruleCovers() function handles wildcard matching (verbs, resources, non-resource URLs) and resource name restrictions.\\n\\n6. **Error Reporting (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/policy_compact.go):** The CompactRules() function consolidates granular missing permission rules into a human-readable format, combining rules that differ only by verb to improve error message clarity.\\n\\n7. **Garbage Collection Handling (pkg/registry/rbac/helpers.go):** The IsOnlyMutatingGCFields() function allows GC-related updates (finalizers, owner references, managed fields) to bypass escalation checks, preventing unnecessary permission escalation denials during object deletion.\\n\\n8. **Admission Policy Integration:** Additional authorization checks in mutatingadmissionpolicy/authz.go and mutatingadmissionpolicybinding/authz.go use EscalationAllowed() to bypass checks for superusers, maintaining consistency across admission control.\\n\\nThe escalation checking flow is: User attempts to create/modify a role or binding \u2192 Storage layer checks if EscalationAllowed (superuser) or RoleEscalationAuthorized (has escalate permission) \u2192 If not, calls ConfirmNoEscalation/ConfirmNoEscalationInternal \u2192 Retrieves user's current permissions via DefaultRuleResolver \u2192 Compares via Covers() using atomic rule breakdown \u2192 Returns forbidden if any permissions are missing, with detailed missing rights information.\\n\\nThis design ensures that the 'escalate' verb acts as a gating mechanism - while normal users cannot grant permissions they don't have, users with explicit 'escalate' permission on roles/clusterroles can grant any permissions, providing a controlled escape hatch for role administrators.\"\n}\n",
